     1→# Per-Agent Program Arguments: Unified Storage, UI, and First-Launch Handling  
     2→  
     3→## Context  
     4→  
     5→PR #162 added the Agent CLI (`aimaestro-agent.sh`) which supports passing CLI arguments to programs via `-- <args>`. PR #163 added a `claudeArgs` field to the Agent Profile UI. However:  
     6→  
     7→1. **The CLI sends `programArgs` (array) but the API silently drops it** — field not in type definitions  
     8→2. **The UI stores `claudeArgs` (string)** — different name/format than the CLI  
     9→3. **The Wake API sends bare `"claude" Enter`** — never appends any arguments  
    10→4. **The Create Wizard doesn't collect CLI arguments**  
    11→5. **Resume flags (--continue, resume --last, --resume) must be skipped on first launch** when no prior session exists  
    12→  
    13→This PR unifies everything under `programArgs` (string) and makes the wake API actually use them.  
    14→  
    15→## Approach: Unified `programArgs` (string)  
    16→  
    17→- **Single field name**: `programArgs` on the Agent — replaces both `claudeArgs` (UI) and the CLI's array format  
    18→- **String format**: Easier to edit in UI, stored as-is, split by shell when passed to tmux  
    19→- **`launchCount`**: Integer on Agent, starts at 0, incremented on each wake — used to detect first launch  
    20→- **Resume pattern stripping**: Per-program regex map strips resume/continue flags when `launchCount === 0`  
    21→  
    22→## Files to Modify  
    23→  
    24→### 1. `types/agent.ts`  
    25→  
    26→**Rename `claudeArgs` → `programArgs`, add `launchCount`:**  
    27→

    29→- Line ~175: Add `launchCount?: number` with comment: `// Number of times agent has been woken/launched (0 = never launched)`

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/.claude/plans/enchanted-riding-pixel.md has been updated. Here's the result of running `cat -n` on a snippet of the edited file:  
     1→# Team Governance: Messaging Isolation, Role-Based ACL, and Closed Teams  
     2→  
     3→## Context  
     4→  
     5→AI Maestro currently has **ZERO authentication or access control** across all team, task, document, and messaging routes. Any agent can message any other agent, join any team, and access any team's kanban/tasks/documents. This creates chaos when multiple agent groups work on different projects -- agents receive irrelevant messages, wrong directives, and can accidentally interfere with other teams' workflows.  
     6→  
     7→This plan introduces a governance layer with two team types (open/closed), two privileged roles (MANAGER and CHIEF-OF-STAFF), messaging isolation for closed teams, and ACL guards on team resources (kanban, tasks, documents).  
     8→  
     9→**Key design principle:** Open teams preserve ALL current behavior. Governance only applies to closed teams.  
    10→  
    11→## User Requirements Summary  
    12→  
    13→1. **Two team types:** `open` (current behavior) and `closed` (messaging isolation + ACL)  
    14→2. **MANAGER:** Global singleton. Can message anyone, manage all teams, belong to multiple teams  
    15→3. **CHIEF-OF-STAFF (COS):** Per-team leader of a closed team. Can communicate cross-team with other COS agents and MANAGER. Can manage their own team  
    16→4. **Normal agents in closed teams:** Can ONLY message members of their own closed team. Limited to ONE closed team at a time  
    17→5. **Forced transfer:** When assigned to a closed team, agent auto-leaves any previous closed team  
    18→6. **Kanban/task/document ACL:** Only members of a closed team (plus MANAGER and COS) can see/use that team's resources  
    19→7. **Password protection:** Only the user can assign MANAGER/COS roles, authenticated by a bcrypt-hashed password  
    20→8. **Password recovery (Phase 2):** O  

... [17833 more chars truncated]

     1→# Agent Messaging Protocol (AMP)  
     2→  
     3→Send and receive messages with other AI agents using the Agent Messaging Protocol.  
     4→  
     5→---  
     6→  
     7→## ⚠️ IMPORTANT: Identity Check (Run First)  
     8→  
     9→**Before using any messaging commands, ALWAYS verify your identity:**  
    10→  
    11→```bash  
    12→amp-identity  
    13→```  
    14→  
    15→If you see "Not initialized", run:  
    16→```bash  
    17→amp-init --auto  
    18→```  
    19→  
    20→This identity check is essential because:  
    21→- Your AMP identity persists across sessions  
    22→- After context reset, you need to rediscover who you are  
    23→- Each agent has its own isolated AMP directory with identity, keys, and messages  
    24→  
    25→**Your identity file location:** `${AMP_DIR}/IDENTITY.md` (per-agent, auto-resolved)  
    26→  
    27→---  
    28→  
    29→## Overview  
    30→  
    31→AMP is a secure messaging protocol for AI agents. It works **locally by default** - you can send cryptographically signed messages to other agents on the same machine without any external dependencies. Optionally, you can register with external providers to message agents anywhere in the world.  
    32→  
    33→## Quick Start  
    34→  
    35→### 1. Initialize (first time only)  
    36→  
    37→```bash  
    38→amp-init --auto  
    39→```  
    40→  
    41→### 2. Send a message  
    42→  
    43→```bash  
    44→amp-send alice "Hello" "How are you?"  
    45→```  
    46→  
    47→### 3. Check inbox  
    48→  
    49→```bash  
    50→amp-inbox  
    51→```  
    52→  
    53→## Address Formats  
    54→  
    55→**Local addresses** (work within your AI Maestro mesh):  
    56→- `alice` → `alice@<your-org>.aimaestro.local`  
    57→- `bob@acme.aimaestro.local` → Local delivery within acme organization  
    58→  
    59→The organization name is automatically fetched from AI Maestro during initialization.  
    60→  
    61→**External addresses** (require registration):  
    62→- `alice@acme.crabmail.ai` → Via Crabmail provider  
    63→- `backend-api@23block

   # Check governance status and your role

   | Delete closed team | MANAGER only | `DELETE /api/teams/{id}` (include `X-Agent-Id` header) |
   | Change team type open->closed | MANAGER only | `PUT /api/teams/{id}`

User has approved your plan. You can now start coding. Start with updating your todo list if applicable  

Your plan has been saved to: /Users/emanuelesabetta/.claude/plans/enchanted-riding-pixel.md  
You can refer back to it if needed during implementation.  

## Approved Plan:  
# Team Governance: Messaging Isolation, Role-Based ACL, and Closed Teams  

## Context  

AI Maestro currently has **ZERO authentication or access control** across all team, task, document, and messaging routes. Any agent can message any other agent, join any team, and access any team's kanban/tasks/documents. This creates chaos when multiple agent groups work on different projects -- agents receive irrelevant messages, wrong directives, and can accidentally interfere with other teams' workflows.  

This plan introduces a governance layer with two team types (open/closed), two privileged roles (MANAGER and CHIEF-OF-STAFF), messaging isolation for closed teams, and ACL guards on team resources (kanban, tasks, documents).  

**Key design principle:** Open teams preserve ALL current behavior. Governance only applies to closed teams.  

## User Requirements Summary  

1. **Two team types:** `open` (current behavior) and `closed` (messaging isolation + ACL)  
2. **MANAGER:** Global singleton. Can message anyone, manage all teams, belong to multiple teams  
3. **CHIEF-OF-STAFF (COS):** Per-team leader of a closed team. Can communicate cross-team with other COS agents and MANAGER. Can manage their own team  
4. **Normal agents in closed teams:** Can ONLY message members of their own closed team. Limited to ONE closed team at a time  
5. **Forced transfer:** When assigned to a closed team, agent auto-leaves any previous closed team  
6. **Kanban/task/document ACL:** Only members of a closed team (plus MANAGER and COS) can see/use that team's resources  
7. **Password protection:** Only the user can assign MANAGER/COS roles, authenticated by a bcrypt-hashed password  
8. **Password recovery (Phase 2):** OS-native notifications (mac  

... [22328 more chars truncated]  

</details>

## <span style="color:#FFC107">◇ ASSISTANT</span>  *[2026-02-16 11:23:47]*

<details>
<summary>🔧 Tool: Edit -- `team.ts`</summary>

**Input:**

**File:** `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/team.ts`  

**Old:**  
```
/**
 * Team types for the Team Meeting feature
 *
 * Teams represent groups of agents that can be assembled into
 * a "war room" for multi-agent coordination sessions.
 */

export interface Team {
  id: string              // UUID
  name: string            // "Backend Squad"
  description?: string
  agentIds: string[]      // Agent UUIDs (order = display order)
  instructions?: string   // Team-level markdown (like a per-team CLAUDE.md)

}
```

**New:**  
```
/**
 * Team types for the Team Meeting feature
 *
 * Teams represent groups of agents that can be assembled into
 * a "war room" for multi-agent coordination sessions.
 *
 * Teams can be 'open' (default, current behavior) or 'closed'
 * (messaging isolation + ACL on resources).
 */

import type { TeamType } from './governance'

export interface Team {
  id: string              // UUID
  name: string            // "Backend Squad"
  description?: string
  agentIds: string[]      // Agent UUIDs (order = display order)
  instructions?: string   // Team-level markdown (like a per-team CLAUDE.md)
  type?: TeamType         // 'open' (default) or 'closed' — governs messaging isolation and ACL
  chiefOfStaffId?: string // Agent UUID of this team's Chief-of-Staff (only meaningful for closed teams)
  createdAt: string       // ISO
  updatedAt: string       // ISO
  lastMeetingAt?: string  // ISO - last time a meeting was started with this team
  lastActivityAt?: string // ISO - updated on any team interaction
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/team.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→

    11→  
    12→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    13→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    14→  recipientAgentId: string  
    15→  isMeshForwarded?: boolean  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm:  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    36→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    37→  
    38→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    39→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    40→    return { allowed: true }  
    41→  }  
    42→  
    43→  // Load team membership for both parties  
    44→  const senderTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(senderAgentId)  
    45→  const recipientTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(recipientAgentId)  
    46→  
    47→  // Step 2: Neither party is in a closed team — open world, all

     1→/**  
     2→ * Team Resource ACL — checks whether an agent (or web UI request)  
     3→ * is allowed to access a given team's resources.  
     4→ *

    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}

    25→ *  
    26→ * Decision order:  
    27→ *  1. Web UI (no agentId)      → allowed  
    28→ *  2. Team not found           → allowed (caller handles 404)  
    29→ *  3. Team is open / untyped   → allowed  
    30→ *  4. Requester is MANAGER     → allowed  
    31→ *  5. Requester is chief-of-staff → allowed  
    32→ *  6. Requester is a member    → allowed  
    33→ *  7. Otherwise                → denied  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult {  
    36→  // 1. Web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always pass  
    37→  if (input.requestingAgentId === undefined) {  
    38→    return { allowed: true }  
    39→  }  
    40→  
    41→  // 2. Team not found — let the caller deal with 404  
    42→  const team = getTeam(input.teamId)  
    43→  if (!team) {  
    44→    return { allowed: true }  
    45→  }  
    46→  
    47→  // 3. Open teams (or teams with no explicit type) have no ACL  
    48→  if (team.type !== 'closed') {  
    49→    return { allowed: true }  
    50→  }  
    51→  
    52→  // 4. MANAGER role always has access  
    53→  if (isManager(input.requestingAgentId)) {  
    54→    return { allowed: true }  
    55→  }  
    56→  
    57→  // 5.

     1→# Agent Messaging Protocol (AMP)  
     2→  
     3→Send and receive messages with other AI agents using the Agent Messaging Protocol.  
     4→  
     5→---  
     6→  
     7→## ⚠️ IMPORTANT: Identity Check (Run First)  
     8→  
     9→**Before using any messaging commands, ALWAYS verify your identity:**  
    10→  
    11→```bash  
    12→amp-identity  
    13→```  
    14→  
    15→If you see "Not initialized", run:  
    16→```bash  
    17→amp-init --auto  
    18→```  
    19→  
    20→This identity check is essential because:  
    21→- Your AMP identity persists across sessions  
    22→- After context reset, you need to rediscover who you are  
    23→- Each agent has its own isolated AMP directory with identity, keys, and messages  
    24→  
    25→**Your identity file location:** `${AMP_DIR}/IDENTITY.md` (per-agent, auto-resolved)  
    26→  
    27→---  
    28→  
    29→## Overview  
    30→  
    31→AMP is a secure messaging protocol for AI agents. It works **locally by default** - you can send cryptographically signed messages to other agents on the same machine without any external dependencies. Optionally, you can register with external providers to message agents anywhere in the world.  
    32→  
    33→## Quick Start  
    34→

    26→---  
    27→  
    28→## Core Principle  
    29→  
    30→```  
    31→Context Window = RAM (volatile, limited, fast)  
    32→Filesystem = Disk (persistent, unlimited, explicit read required)  
    33→  
    34→Anything important gets written to disk.  
    35→```

**Body sections:**  

1. `# Team Governance` - title  

2. `## Role Check (Run First)` - Agent must verify its role:  
   ```bash
   curl -s "http://localhost:23000/api/governance" | jq .
   ```
   If agent is not MANAGER or COS of any team, STOP and inform user.  

3. `## Team Management` - table of operations:  
   - List teams: GET /api/teams  
   - Create open team: POST /api/teams with { name, type: "open" }  
   - Create closed team (MANAGER only): POST /api/teams with { name, type: "closed" } + X-Agent-Id header  
   - Delete closed team (MANAGER only): DELETE /api/teams/{id} + X-Agent-Id header  
   - Change type open->closed (MANAGER only): PUT /api/teams/{id} with { type: "closed" } + X-Agent-Id header  
   - Change type closed->open (MANAGER only): PUT /api/teams/{id} with { type: "open" } + X-Agent-Id header  
   Include curl examples for each.  

4. `## Agent Assignment` - table of operations:  
   - Assign agent to closed team (MANAGER or COS of that team): PUT /api/teams/{id} with updated agentIds[] + X-Agent-Id header  
   - Remove agent from closed team: same PUT with agent removed  
   - Transfer agent (MANAGER only, cross-team): assign to new team, old membership auto-removed  
   Include curl examples.  

5. `## Chief-of-Staff Assignment` (MANAGER only):  
   - Assign COS: POST /api/teams/{id}/chief-of-staff with { agentId, password }  
   - Remove COS: POST /api/teams/{id}/chief-of-staff with { agentId: null, password }  
   Note: requires governance password from user.  

6. `## Broadcast Messages` - how to broadcast:  
   - COS broadcasts to own team: loop agentIds, amp-send to each  
   - MANAGER broadcasts to any team: same loop  
   Include bash snippet:  
   ```bash
   TEAM_ID="<team-uuid>"
   AGENTS=$(curl -s "http://localhost:23000/api/teams/$TEAM_ID" | jq -r '.agentIds[]')
   for AGENT_ID in $AGENTS; do
     AGENT_NAME=$(curl -s "http://localhost:23000/api/agents/$AGENT_ID" | jq -r '.name')
     amp-send "$AGENT_NAME" "Team Update" "Your message here"
   done
   ```

7. `## Permission Matrix` - markdown table:  
   | Action | Normal Agent | COS (own team) | COS (other team) | MANAGER |  
   With rows for: create open/closed team, delete open/closed team, change type, assign/remove age

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-16 11:25:06]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Create the file `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/team-acl.ts`. This is a team resource ACL check for AI Maestro (Next.js 14, TypeScript).  

Read `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/team.ts` for Team type.  

The file must export:  

```typescript
export interface TeamAccessInput {
  teamId: string
  requestingAgentId?: string   // undefined = web UI request (always allowed)
}

export interface TeamAccessResult {
  allowed: boolean
  reason?: string
}

export function checkTeamAccess(input: TeamAccessInput): TeamAccessResult
```

Algorithm for `checkTeamAccess`:  
1. If `requestingAgentId` is undefined: return `{ allowed: true }` — web UI requests (no X-Agent-Id header) always have access  
2. Load team via `getTeam(teamId)`. If team is null: return `{ allowed: true }` — let the caller handle 404  
3. If team type is not 'closed' (i.e. undefined or 'open'): return `{ allowed: true }` — open teams have no ACL  
4. If `isManager(requestingAgentId)`: return `{ allowed: true }`  
5. If team.chiefOfStaffId === requestingAgentId: return `{ allowed: true }`  
6. If `team.agentIds.includes(requestingAgentId)`: return `{ allowed: true }`  
7. Otherwise: return `{ allowed: false, reason: 'Access denied: you are not a member of this closed team' }`  

Import from governance.ts: `import { isManager } from './governance'`  
Import from team-registry: `import { getTeam } from './team-registry'`  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - one-line result"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator  

</div>

     6→ */  
     7→  
     8→import fs from 'fs'  
     9→import path from 'path'  
    10→import os from 'os'  
    11→import { v4 as uuidv4 } from 'uuid'

    16→const TEAMS_FILE = path.join(TEAMS_DIR, 'teams.json')  
    17→  
    18→function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    19→  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    20→    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    21→  }  
    22→}  
    23→  
    24→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
    25→  try {  
    26→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    27→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
    28→      return []  
    29→    }  
    30→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    31→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    32→    return Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
    33→  } catch (error) {  
    34→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
    35→    return []  
    36→  }  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→export function saveTeams(teams: Team[]): boolean {  
    40→  try {  
    41→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    42→    const file: TeamsFile = { version: 1, teams }  
    43→    fs.writeFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    44→    return true  
    45→  } catch (error) {  
    46→    console.error('Failed to save teams:', error)  
    47→    return false  
    48→  }  
    49→}  
    50→  
    51→export function getTeam(id: string): Team | null {  
    52→  const teams = loadTeams()  
    53→  return teams.find(t => t.id === id) || null  
    54→}  
    55→  
    56→export function createTeam(data: { name: string; description?: string; agentIds: string[] }): Team {

Create the file `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts`. This is a governance library for the AI Maestro project (Next.js 14, TypeScript).  

Read `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/governance.ts` for the types to import.  
Read `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/team-registry.ts` to understand the file I/O pattern (loadTeams, saveTeams, ensureTeamsDir, etc.) — follow the same patterns.  

The file must export these functions:  

1. `loadGovernance(): GovernanceConfig` — reads `~/.aimaestro/governance.json`, creates with DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG if missing  
2. `saveGovernance(config: GovernanceConfig): boolean` — writes governance.json  
3. `setPassword(plaintext: string): void` — bcrypt hash with salt rounds 12, saves to governance.json  
4. `verifyPassword(plaintext: string): boolean` — bcrypt compare against stored hash, returns false if no password set  
5. `getManagerId(): string | null` — returns managerId from governance config  
6. `setManager(agentId: string): void` — sets managerId in governance config and saves  
7. `removeManager(): void` — sets managerId to null and saves  
8. `isManager(agentId: string): boolean` — checks if agentId matches managerId  
9. `isChiefOfStaff(agentId: string, teamId: string): boolean` — loads team via getTeam(teamId), checks team.chiefOfStaffId === agentId  
10. `isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(agentId: string): boolean` — loads all teams, checks if any closed team has chiefOfStaffId === agentId  
11. `getClosedTeamForAgent(agentId: string): Team | null` — loads all teams, returns the first closed team where agentIds includes agentId (normal agents can only be in one)  
12. `getClosedTeamsForAgent(agentId: string): Team[]` — same but returns all (for MANAGER/COS who can be in multiple)  

Import bcryptjs with: `import bcrypt from 'bcryptjs'`  
Import from team-registry: `import { loadTeams, getTeam } from './team-registry'`  
Import from types: `import type { GovernanceConfig } from '@/types/governance'`, `import { DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG } from '@/types/governance'`, `import type { Team } from '@/types/team'`  

Storage path: `path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'governance.json')`  

Use `fs.readFileSync`/`fs.writeFileSync` with `fs.mkdirSync` for the directory — same synchronous pattern as team-registry.ts.  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - one-line result"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator

    17→  
    18→function ensureTeamsDir() {  
    19→  if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_DIR)) {  
    20→    fs.mkdirSync(TEAMS_DIR, { recursive: true })  
    21→  }  
    22→}  
    23→  
    24→export function loadTeams(): Team[] {  
    25→  try {  
    26→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    27→    if (!fs.existsSync(TEAMS_FILE)) {  
    28→      return []  
    29→    }  
    30→    const data = fs.readFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    31→    const parsed: TeamsFile = JSON.parse(data)  
    32→    return Array.isArray(parsed.teams) ? parsed.teams : []  
    33→  } catch (error) {  
    34→    console.error('Failed to load teams:', error)  
    35→    return []  
    36→  }  
    37→}  
    38→  
    39→export function saveTeams(teams: Team[]): boolean {  
    40→  try {  
    41→    ensureTeamsDir()  
    42→    const file: TeamsFile = { version: 1, teams }  
    43→    fs.writeFileSync(TEAMS_FILE, JSON.stringify(file, null, 2), 'utf-8')  
    44→    return true  
    45→  } catch (error) {  
    46→    console.error('Failed to save teams:', error)  
    47→    return false  
    48→  }  
    49→}  
    50→  
    51→export function getTeam(id: string): Team | null {  
    52→  const teams = loadTeams()  
    53→  return teams.find(t => t.id === id) || null  
    54→}

     1→/**  
     2→ * Governance utilities — loads ~/.aimaestro/governance.json  
     3→ * and exposes role-check helpers used by ACL modules.  
     4→ */  
     5→  
     6→import fs from 'fs'  
     7→import path from 'path'  
     8→import os from 'os'  
     9→import type { GovernanceConfig } from '@/types/governance'  
    10→import { DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG } from '@/types/governance'  
    11→  
    12→const GOVERNANCE_FILE = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'governance.json')  
    13→  
    14→/** Load the governance config from disk (returns defaults if missing or corrupt). */  
    15→export function loadGovernanceConfig(): GovernanceConfig {  
    16→  try {  
    17→    if (!fs.existsSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE)) {  
    18→      return { ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }  
    19→    }  
    20→    const data = fs.readFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    21→    return JSON.parse(data) as GovernanceConfig  
    22→  } catch {  
    23→    return { ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }  
    24→  }  
    25→}  
    26→  
    27→/** Returns true when the given agentId is the designated MANAGER. */  
    28→export function isManager(agentId: string): boolean {  
    29→  const config = loadGovernanceConfig()  
    30→  // No manager configured means nobody is a manager  
    31→  if (!config.managerId) return false  
    32→  return config.managerId === agentId  
    33→}  
    34→

## <span style="color:#2196F3">◆ USER</span>  *[2026-02-16 11:25:06]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #2196F3; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

Create the file `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/message-filter.ts`. This is a message filter for the AI Maestro team governance system (Next.js 14, TypeScript).  

Read `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/governance.ts` for governance types.  
Read `/Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/types/team.ts` for Team type.  

The file must export these types and functions:  

```typescript
export interface MessageFilterInput {
  senderAgentId: string | null   // null = mesh-forwarded message
  recipientAgentId: string
  isMeshForwarded?: boolean
}

export interface MessageFilterResult {
  allowed: boolean
  reason?: string
}

export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult
```

The `checkMessageAllowed` algorithm (implement this exactly):  
1. If `senderAgentId` is null (mesh-forwarded): return `{ allowed: true }` — trust mesh peers  
2. Load sender's closed team and recipient's closed team using governance helpers  
3. If neither sender nor recipient is in any closed team: return `{ allowed: true }` — open world, current behavior  
4. If sender is MANAGER (check via `isManager(senderAgentId)`): return `{ allowed: true }`  
5. If sender is COS of any closed team (`isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(senderAgentId)`):  
   - If recipient is MANAGER: ALLOW  
   - If recipient is COS of any closed team: ALLOW (COS-to-COS bridge)  
   - If recipient is member of sender's own closed team: ALLOW  
   - Otherwise: DENY with reason "Chief-of-Staff can only message MANAGER, other Chiefs-of-Staff, and own team members"  
6. If sender is in a closed team (normal agent):  
   - If recipient is member of same closed team: ALLOW  
   - If recipient is COS of sender's team: ALLOW  
   - Otherwise: DENY with reason "Closed team members can only message within their team"  
7. If sender is NOT in any closed team but recipient IS in a closed team: DENY with reason "Cannot message agents in closed teams from outside"  
8. Default: ALLOW  

Import from governance.ts: `import { isManager, isChiefOfStaffAnywhere, getClosedTeamForAgent } from './governance'`  
Import from team-registry: `import { loadTeams } from './team-registry'`  

REPORTING RULES:  
- Return to orchestrator ONLY: "[DONE/FAILED] task - one-line result"  
- Max 2 lines of text back to orchestrator  

</div>

    45→  } catch (error) {  
    46→    console.error('Failed to save teams:', error)  
    47→    return false  
    48→  }  
    49→}

     1→/**  
     2→ * Governance utilities — loads ~/.aimaestro/governance.json  
     3→ * and exposes role-check helpers used by ACL modules.  
     4→ */  
     5→  
     6→import fs from 'fs'  
     7→import path from 'path'  
     8→import os from 'os'  
     9→import type { GovernanceConfig } from '@/types/governance'  
    10→import { DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG } from '@/types/governance'  
    11→  
    12→const GOVERNANCE_FILE = path.join(os.homedir(), '.aimaestro', 'governance.json')  
    13→  
    14→/** Load the governance config from disk (returns defaults if missing or corrupt). */  
    15→export function loadGovernanceConfig(): GovernanceConfig {  
    16→  try {  
    17→    if (!fs.existsSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE)) {  
    18→      return { ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }  
    19→    }  
    20→    const data = fs.readFileSync(GOVERNANCE_FILE, 'utf-8')  
    21→    return JSON.parse(data) as GovernanceConfig  
    22→  } catch {  
    23→    return { ...DEFAULT_GOVERNANCE_CONFIG }  
    24→  }  
    25→}  
    26→  
    27→/** Returns true when the given agentId is the designated MANAGER. */  
    28→export function isManager(agentId: string): boolean {  
    29→  const config = loadGovernanceConfig()  
    30→  // No manager configured means nobody is a manager  
    31→  if (!config.managerId) return false  
    32→  return config.managerId === agentId  
    33→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-02-16 11:26:27]*

```
/** Returns true when the given agentId is the designated MANAGER. */
export function isManager(agentId: string): boolean {

  if (!config.managerId) return false

```

**New:**  
```
/** Returns true when the given agentId is the designated MANAGER. */
export function isManager(agentId: string): boolean {
  const config = loadGovernanceConfig()
  // No manager configured means nobody is a manager
  if (!config.managerId) return false
  return config.managerId === agentId
}

/** Returns true when the given agentId is Chief-of-Staff of any closed team. */
export function isChiefOfStaffAnywhere(agentId: string): boolean {
  const teams = loadTeams()
  return teams.some(
    (t) => t.type === 'closed' && t.chiefOfStaffId === agentId
  )
}

/** Return the closed team that agentId belongs to (as member via agentIds), or null. */
export function getClosedTeamForAgent(agentId: string): Team | null {
  const teams = loadTeams()
  return (
    teams.find(
      (t) => t.type === 'closed' && t.agentIds.includes(agentId)
    ) ?? null
  )
}

/** Return all closed teams where agentId is Chief-of-Staff. */
export function getClosedTeamsWhereCoS(agentId: string): Team[] {
  const teams = loadTeams()
  return teams.filter(
    (t) => t.type === 'closed' && t.chiefOfStaffId === agentId
  )
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/lib/governance.ts has been updated successfully.  

</details>

```
/**
 * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation
 *
 * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed

 * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message
 * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.

export interface MessageFilterInput {
  senderAgentId: string | null // n
```

**Result:**

     1→/**  
     2→ * Message Filter — enforces closed-team messaging isolation  
     3→ *  
     4→ * Determines whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed  
     5→ * based on governance roles (MANAGER, Chief-of-Staff) and closed-team  
     6→ * membership. Open-world agents (not in any closed team) can message  
     7→ * freely unless the recipient is inside a closed team.  
     8→ */  
     9→  
    10→import { isManager, isChiefOfStaffAnywhere, getClosedTeamForAgent } from './governance'  
    11→  
    12→export interface MessageFilterInput {  
    13→  senderAgentId: string | null // null = mesh-forwarded message  
    14→  recipientAgentId: string  
    15→  isMeshForwarded?: boolean  
    16→}  
    17→  
    18→export interface MessageFilterResult {  
    19→  allowed: boolean  
    20→  reason?: string  
    21→}  
    22→  
    23→/**  
    24→ * Check whether a message from sender to recipient is allowed.  
    25→ *  
    26→ * Algorithm:  
    27→ * 1. Mesh-forwarded (senderAgentId null): always allowed (trust mesh peers)  
    28→ * 2. Neither in a closed team: allowed (open world, current behavior)  
    29→ * 3. Sender is MANAGER: always allowed  
    30→ * 4. Sender is COS of any closed team: can reach MANAGER, other COS, own team members  
    31→ * 5. Normal closed-team member: can reach same-team members and own COS  
    32→ * 6. Outside sender to closed-team recipient: denied  
    33→ * 7. Default: allowed  
    34→ */  
    35→export function checkMessageAllowed(input: MessageFilterInput): MessageFilterResult {  
    36→  const { senderAgentId, recipientAgentId } = input  
    37→  
    38→  // Step 1: Mesh-forwarded messages are always trusted  
    39→  if (senderAgentId === null) {  
    40→    return { allowed: true }  
    41→  }  
    42→  
    43→  // Load team membership for both parties  
    44→  const senderTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(senderAgentId)  
    45→  const recipientTeam = getClosedTeamForAgent(recipientAgentId)  
    46→  
    47→  // Step 2: Neither party is in a closed team — open world, all  

... [2108 more chars truncated]  

</details>
